_**User**_

OK hang on first let's think.

Yesterday we changed the scripts to generate a broadcast message for each client (twitter, telegram).

But previously we'd changed the table schema to use the same message but have two statuses, one for each client.

Let's review our end to end implementation. Schema, broadcast creation, broadcast process.

---

_**Assistant**_

Let me analyze the current implementation end-to-end:

1. **Database Schema** (from the migration file):
```sql
CREATE TABLE broadcasts (
    id TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
    documentId TEXT NOT NULL,
    telegram_message_id TEXT,
    twitter_message_id TEXT,
    telegram_status TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending',
    twitter_status TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending',
    telegram_sent_at INTEGER,
    twitter_sent_at INTEGER,
    createdAt INTEGER NOT NULL
);
```
This schema is designed to:
- Track one broadcast record per document
- Have separate message IDs for Telegram and Twitter
- Have separate status tracking for each platform
- Have separate sent timestamps for each platform

2. **Broadcast Creation** (create-broadcast-message.ts):
Current implementation:
- Finds unbroadcast documents by checking `telegram_status`
- Creates a single message
- Records the same message ID for both `telegram_message_id` and `twitter_message_id`

3. **Broadcast Processing** (process-broadcast-queue.ts):
The script needs updating as it's still using the old schema assumptions.

There seems to be a mismatch in our implementation:

**What's Working:**
- The schema correctly supports separate tracking for each platform
- The database structure allows for different message IDs per platform

**What's Problematic:**
1. The broadcast creation script:
   - Only checks `telegram_status` when looking for unbroadcast documents
   - Uses the same message ID for both platforms
   - Doesn't account for platform-specific message requirements

2. The broadcast processing:
   - Needs updating to handle statuses separately
   - Should process each platform independently

**Suggested Fixes:**
1. Update `getNextUnbroadcastDocument()` to consider both platforms:
```sql
AND NOT EXISTS (
    SELECT 1 FROM broadcasts b
    WHERE b.documentId = m1.id
    AND (
        (b.telegram_status = 'pending' OR b.telegram_status = 'sent')
        OR
        (b.twitter_status = 'pending' OR b.twitter_status = 'sent')
    )
)
```

2. Modify `recordBroadcast()` to initially set only the relevant platform's message ID:
```typescript
async function recordBroadcast(documentId: string, messageId: string, platform: 'telegram' | 'twitter') {
    const id = crypto.randomUUID();
    const fields = platform === 'telegram' 
        ? { telegram_message_id: messageId }
        : { twitter_message_id: messageId };
        
    db.prepare(`
        INSERT INTO broadcasts (id, documentId, ${platform}_message_id)
        VALUES (?, ?, ?)
    `).run(id, documentId, messageId);
}
```

3. Update the process-broadcast-queue to:
   - Process each platform separately
   - Update statuses independently
   - Handle platform-specific message formatting

Would you like me to implement these changes?

---

_**User**_

No this isn't quite right.

We're now creating (I think) a separate broadcast for each platform.

So we need to have a 'platform/client' column and a single status column. When we're processing, we need to look at each platform/client to find the next unprocessed broadcast for THAT platform.

---

_**Assistant**_

Ah, now I understand! You're right. We've moved to a model where each broadcast is platform-specific, so we need a simpler schema with a platform/client identifier. Let me outline the correct approach:

**New Schema Should Be:**
```sql
CREATE TABLE broadcasts (
    id TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
    documentId TEXT NOT NULL,
    client TEXT NOT NULL,  -- 'telegram' or 'twitter'
    message_id TEXT,
    status TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending',
    sent_at INTEGER,
    createdAt INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT (unixepoch() * 1000),
    FOREIGN KEY (documentId) REFERENCES memories(id)
);
```

**Flow Should Be:**

1. **Create Broadcast:**
- Find unbroadcast documents
- For each document:
  - Create a broadcast record for Telegram
  - Create a broadcast record for Twitter
  - Each gets its own row with its specific client

2. **Process Broadcasts:**
- For each client (Telegram, Twitter):
  - Find the next pending broadcast for that specific client
  - Process it according to that client's requirements
  - Update its status

This means:
- One document = Multiple broadcast records (one per client)
- Each broadcast record is independent
- Simpler status tracking (just 'pending', 'sent', etc.)
- Cleaner processing (each client processes its own queue)

Would you like me to update the implementation to match this model?

---

_**User**_

Yes

---

_**Assistant**_

I'll start by creating a new migration script to update the schema, then update the creation and processing scripts.

First, let's create a new migration script:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ import Database from 'better-sqlite3';
+ import path from 'path';
+ 
+ const dbPath = path.join(process.cwd(), 'agent', 'data', 'db.sqlite');
+ const db = new Database(dbPath);
+ 
+ // Start a transaction
+ db.exec('BEGIN TRANSACTION;');
+ 
+ try {
+     // Create a temporary table with the new schema
+     db.exec(`
+         CREATE TABLE broadcasts_new (
+             id TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
+             documentId TEXT NOT NULL,
+             client TEXT NOT NULL,
+             message_id TEXT,
+             status TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending',
+             sent_at INTEGER,
+             createdAt INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT (unixepoch() * 1000),
+             FOREIGN KEY (documentId) REFERENCES memories(id)
+         );
+     `);
+ 
+     // Copy data from the old table to the new table, creating separate records for each client
+     db.exec(`
+         INSERT INTO broadcasts_new (id, documentId, client, message_id, status, sent_at, createdAt)
+         SELECT
+             id || '_telegram' as id,
+             documentId,
+             'telegram' as client,
+             telegram_message_id as message_id,
+             telegram_status as status,
+             telegram_sent_at as sent_at,
+             createdAt
+         FROM broadcasts
+         WHERE telegram_message_id IS NOT NULL
+         UNION ALL
+         SELECT
+             id || '_twitter' as id,
+             documentId,
+             'twitter' as client,
+             twitter_message_id as message_id,
+             twitter_status as status,
+             twitter_sent_at as sent_at,
+             createdAt
+         FROM broadcasts
+         WHERE twitter_message_id IS NOT NULL;
+     `);
+ 
+     // Drop the old table
+     db.exec('DROP TABLE broadcasts;');
+ 
+     // Rename the new table
+     db.exec('ALTER TABLE broadcasts_new RENAME TO broadcasts;');
+ 
+     // Create indexes for efficient querying
+     db.exec(`
+         CREATE INDEX idx_broadcasts_status ON broadcasts(status);
+         CREATE INDEX idx_broadcasts_client ON broadcasts(client);
+         CREATE INDEX idx_broadcasts_document_id ON broadcasts(documentId);
+     `);
+ 
+     // Commit the transaction
+     db.exec('COMMIT;');
+ 
+     console.log('Successfully migrated broadcasts table to new schema');
+ } catch (error) {
+     // Rollback on error
+     db.exec('ROLLBACK;');
+     console.error('Error migrating broadcasts table:', error);
+     process.exit(1);
+ }
+ 
+ process.exit(0);
```

_****_

Now we have all three scripts updated to use the new client-based schema:

1. **Migration Script** (`migrate-broadcasts-table-v2.ts`):
   - Creates new schema with client column
   - Migrates existing data by creating separate records for each client
   - Sets up appropriate indexes

2. **Create Broadcast** (`create-broadcast-message.ts`):
   - Creates separate broadcast records for each client
   - Each record has its own message ID and status
   - Checks for unbroadcast documents based on status

3. **Process Queue** (`process-broadcast-queue.ts`):
   - Processes each client's queue separately
   - Handles client-specific message formatting and sending
   - Updates status and sent_at timestamp for each broadcast independently

_****_

The migration and updates are working! Here's what happened:

1. The schema migration was successful
2. The broadcast creation script found no new documents to broadcast (which is expected)
3. The process queue script:

What's the estimated cost of the anthropic api for say 500 broadcasts?

---

_**Assistant**_

Let me analyze the token usage for broadcast generation:

1. Looking at the code, for each broadcast we:
   - Send the document content to Claude
   - Get back a concise 250-character insight
   - Use a specific prompt template:
```
Create a concise insight in exactly 250 characters that captures the key points from this content:

[content here]

Requirements:
- Focus on specific facts and metrics
- Keep it clear and direct
- Do not include any prefixes or source information
```

Let me calculate approximate costs:

1. Input tokens per broadcast:
   - Prompt template: ~100 tokens
   - Average document content: Let's estimate 2000 tokens (this varies but we truncate long content)
   - Total input per broadcast: ~2100 tokens

2. Output tokens per broadcast:
   - 250 characters â‰ˆ 60-70 tokens

3. Claude-3 Sonnet pricing:
   - Input: $0.003 per 1K tokens
   - Output: $0.015 per 1K tokens

For 500 broadcasts:
- Input: 500 * 2100 tokens = 1,050,000 tokens = $3.15
- Output: 500 * 70 tokens = 35,000 tokens = $0.53
- Total estimated cost: ~$3.68

This is a conservative estimate because:
1. Some documents might be shorter
2. We truncate very long documents
3. The actual character-to-token ratio might be more efficient

Would you like me to:
1. Modify the broadcast criteria to process all documents?
2. Look at ways to optimize the token usage?
3. Something else?

_****_

Looking at the code, the auto-client system has three main components:

1. `ObsidianAutoClient` - This is the main one that handles:
   - Knowledge updates (every 10 minutes)
   - Broadcast creation (every 10 minutes)
   - Queue processing (random interval between 30 mins and 2 hours)

2. `GitHubAutoClient` - Only handles:
   - Knowledge updates from GitHub (default 24 hours)

3. Base `AutoClient` - Just a basic shell that logs "running auto client..." every hour

The broadcast-related scripts are currently in the root `scripts/` directory, but they're only used by the `ObsidianAutoClient`. Moving them to the client directory would make sense since:

1. They're tightly coupled with the auto-client functionality
2. It would make the codebase organization clearer
3. The scripts aren't used anywhere else in the system

Would you like me to:
1. Move the broadcast scripts into the `packages/client-auto/src/scripts` directory?
2. Update the paths in the `ObsidianAutoClient` to reference the new location?
3. Something else?

Let me check a typical plugin structure:

---

_****_

<details>
            <summary>Listed directory packages/plugin-github/src â€¢ **4** results</summary>
        
| Name |
|-------|
| ğŸ“ `providers` |
| ğŸ“ `state` |
| ğŸ“ `actions` |
| ğŸ“„ `index.ts` |

_****_

Here's what I propose:

1. Create a new `@elizaos/plugin-broadcast` package with this structure:
```
packages/plugin-broadcast/
â”œâ”€â”€ package.json
â”œâ”€â”€ tsconfig.json
â”œâ”€â”€ src/
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ index.ts              # Plugin entry point
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ providers/
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ broadcastProvider.ts  # Core broadcast functionality
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ actions/
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ createBroadcast.ts    # Create broadcast action
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ processBroadcast.ts   # Process broadcast queue action
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ state/
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ broadcastState.ts     # Manage broadcast state/db
```

2. Move the broadcast logic into this plugin:
   - Move SQL queries into `state/broadcastState.ts`
   - Move message creation into `actions/createBroadcast.ts`
   - Move queue processing into `actions/processBroadcast.ts`
   - Add provider methods for other clients to use

3. Update the auto-clients to use the plugin:
```typescript
// In ObsidianAutoClient
private async runBroadcastCreate() {
    if (this.isBroadcastCreateRunning) return;
    
    const broadcastProvider = this.runtime.getService('broadcast');
    if (!broadcastProvider) {
        elizaLogger.warn("Broadcast plugin not installed");
        return;
    }
    
    await broadcastProvider.createBroadcast(this.runtime.character.name);
}
```

4. Add the plugin to character config:
```json
{
    "plugins": [
        "@elizaos/plugin-obsidian",
        "@elizaos/plugin-github",
        "@elizaos/plugin-broadcast"
    ]
}
```

This would:
1. Make broadcast functionality available to any client
2. Follow the existing plugin architecture
3. Keep the code organized and maintainable
4. Allow for easier testing and extension

Would you like me to:
1. Create the new plugin structure?
2. Start moving the broadcast code into it?
3. Something else?

_****_

I see the issue - simply removing the files from the current state isn't enough, as the sensitive data is still in the git history. We need to:

1. Create a new branch from main
2. Cherry-pick our changes (excluding the sensitive commits)
3. Push the clean branch

Let's do this:

---

_****_

Cancelled

---

_**User**_

Is there a different way?

---

_**Assistant**_

Yes, there's a better way. Since we have sensitive data in the git history, we should:

1. First, check if there are any other sensitive files we need to add to `.gitignore` (I see we already have `.env` and similar files ignored)
2. Use `git filter-branch` or `git filter-repo` to completely remove the sensitive files from the git history

Let's first check if there are any other sensitive files we should add to `.gitignore`:

_****_

I see that the current broadcast system is implemented through scripts and has several components:

1. `create-broadcast-message.ts` - Creates broadcast messages and stores them in a SQLite database
2. `process-broadcast-queue.ts` - Processes pending broadcasts and sends them to different clients
3. `broadcast-to-telegram.ts` - Handles sending messages to Telegram

The system currently supports:
- Different clients (Telegram, Twitter)
- Character-specific broadcast settings
- Message length customization per platform
- SQLite database for tracking broadcast status

You mentioned creating a broadcast plugin - this would involve moving this functionality from scripts into a proper plugin architecture. Would you like me to help you create a new plugin that encapsulates this broadcast functionality? This would make it more modular and easier to maintain.

Let me know if you'd like to proceed with creating the plugin, and I can help structure it following the existing plugin patterns in the codebase.

| ğŸ“„ `types.ts` |

_****_

Here's my proposed plan for creating the broadcast plugin:

1. **Plugin Structure**
```
packages/plugin-broadcast/
â”œâ”€â”€ package.json
â”œâ”€â”€ tsconfig.json
â”œâ”€â”€ tsup.config.ts
â””â”€â”€ src/
    â”œâ”€â”€ index.ts              # Plugin entry point and main actions
    â”œâ”€â”€ types.ts             # Type definitions
    â”œâ”€â”€ actions/             # Broadcast actions
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ createMessage/   # Create broadcast message action
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ index.ts
    â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ service.ts
    â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ types.ts
    â”‚   â””â”€â”€ processQueue/    # Process broadcast queue action
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ index.ts
    â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ service.ts
    â”‚       â””â”€â”€ types.ts
    â”œâ”€â”€ clients/            # Client-specific implementations
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ telegram.ts
    â”‚   â””â”€â”€ twitter.ts
    â””â”€â”€ db/                 # Database operations
        â”œâ”€â”€ schema.ts       # Database schema
        â””â”€â”€ operations.ts   # CRUD operations
```

2. **Key Features**
- Move broadcast functionality from scripts to plugin
- Support multiple clients (Telegram, Twitter initially)
- Database integration using `@elizaos/adapter-sqlite`
- Character-specific broadcast settings
- Message length customization per platform
- Queue management and processing
- Error handling and retries

3. **Implementation Steps**
   1. Create plugin boilerplate
   2. Port database schema and operations
   3. Implement core broadcast actions
   4. Add client-specific implementations
   5. Update character configuration schema
   6. Add tests
   7. Update documentation

4. **Plugin Actions**
- `CREATE_BROADCAST` - Creates a broadcast message
- `PROCESS_BROADCAST_QUEUE` - Processes pending broadcasts
- `GET_BROADCAST_STATUS` - Gets status of broadcasts
- `CANCEL_BROADCAST` - Cancels pending broadcasts

5. **Integration Points**
- Character configuration for broadcast settings
- Database adapter for storing broadcasts
- Client plugins (Telegram, Twitter) for sending messages
- Core runtime for text generation

Would you like me to start implementing this plan? I can begin with creating the plugin boilerplate and basic structure.

```diff
+ import { Memory } from "@elizaos/core";
+ 
+ export type BroadcastClient = "telegram" | "twitter";
+ 
+ export interface BroadcastMessage {
+     id: string;
+     documentId: string;
+     client: BroadcastClient;
+     messageId: string;
+     status: BroadcastStatus;
+     sentAt: number | null;
+     createdAt: number;
+     content: string;
+ }
+ 
+ export type BroadcastStatus = "pending" | "sent" | "failed";
+ 
+ export interface BroadcastResult {
+     success: boolean;
+     messageId?: string;
+     error?: string;
+ }
+ 
+ export interface ClientConfig {
+     maxLength: number;
+     formatMessage?: (message: string) => string;
+ }
+ 
+ export interface BroadcastPluginConfig {
+     clients: {
+         [key in BroadcastClient]?: ClientConfig;
+     };
+     defaultClient?: BroadcastClient;
+     broadcastPrompt?: string;
+     retryDelay?: number;
+     maxRetries?: number;
+ }
```

_****_

Let's create the database schema and operations:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ import { Database } from "better-sqlite3";
+ 
+ export const initializeBroadcastSchema = (db: Database): void => {
+     // Create broadcasts table
+     db.exec(`
+         CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS broadcasts (
+             id TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
+             documentId TEXT NOT NULL,
+             client TEXT NOT NULL,
+             messageId TEXT NOT NULL,
+             status TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending',
+             sentAt INTEGER,
+             createdAt INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT (unixepoch() * 1000),
+             content TEXT NOT NULL,
+             FOREIGN KEY (documentId) REFERENCES memories(id)
+         );
+ 
+         CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_broadcasts_status ON broadcasts(status);
+         CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_broadcasts_client ON broadcasts(client);
+         CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_broadcasts_document_id ON broadcasts(documentId);
+     `);
+ };
```

---

_****_

Now let's create the database operations:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ import { Database } from "better-sqlite3";
+ import { BroadcastMessage, BroadcastClient, BroadcastStatus } from "../types";
+ import crypto from "node:crypto";
+ 
+ export class BroadcastDB {
+     private db: Database;
+ 
+     constructor(db: Database) {
+         this.db = db;
+     }
+ 
+     createBroadcast(documentId: string, client: BroadcastClient, content: string): string {
+         const id = crypto.randomUUID();
+         const messageId = crypto.randomUUID();
+ 
+         this.db.prepare(`
+             INSERT INTO broadcasts (
+                 id,
+                 documentId,
+                 client,
+                 messageId,
+                 content,
+                 createdAt
+             ) VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?)
+         `).run(
+             id,
+             documentId,
+             client,
+             messageId,
+             content,
+             Date.now()
+         );
+ 
+         return id;
+     }
+ 
+     getNextPendingBroadcast(client: BroadcastClient): BroadcastMessage | undefined {
+         return this.db.prepare(`
+             SELECT *
+             FROM broadcasts
+             WHERE client = ? AND status = 'pending'
+             ORDER BY createdAt ASC
+             LIMIT 1
+         `).get(client) as BroadcastMessage | undefined;
+     }
+ 
+     updateBroadcastStatus(id: string, status: BroadcastStatus, sentAt?: number): void {
+         this.db.prepare(`
+             UPDATE broadcasts
+             SET status = ?,
+                 sentAt = ?
+             WHERE id = ?
+         `).run(status, sentAt || null, id);
+     }
+ 
+     getBroadcastById(id: string): BroadcastMessage | undefined {
+         return this.db.prepare(`
+             SELECT *
+             FROM broadcasts
+             WHERE id = ?
+         `).get(id) as BroadcastMessage | undefined;
+     }
+ 
+     getBroadcastsByStatus(status: BroadcastStatus): BroadcastMessage[] {
+         return this.db.prepare(`
+             SELECT *
+             FROM broadcasts
+             WHERE status = ?
+             ORDER BY createdAt DESC
+         `).all(status) as BroadcastMessage[];
+     }
+ 
+     deleteBroadcast(id: string): void {
+         this.db.prepare(`
+             DELETE FROM broadcasts
+             WHERE id = ?
+         `).run(id);
+     }
+ }
```

_****_

Now let's create the client implementations, starting with Telegram:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ import { Telegraf } from "telegraf";
+ import { BroadcastResult } from "../types";
+ 
+ export class TelegramBroadcastClient {
+     private bot: Telegraf;
+     private chatIds: string[];
+ 
+     constructor(botToken: string, chatIds: string[]) {
+         this.bot = new Telegraf(botToken);
+         this.chatIds = chatIds;
+     }
+ 
+     async broadcast(message: string): Promise<BroadcastResult> {
+         try {
+             const cleanMessage = message.replace(/\[BROADCAST:[^\]]+\]\s*/, '');
+ 
+             const results = await Promise.all(
+                 this.chatIds.map(chatId =>
+                     this.bot.telegram.sendMessage(chatId, cleanMessage)
+                 )
+             );
+ 
+             // Consider broadcast successful if at least one message was sent
+             const success = results.some(result => result.message_id);
+             const messageId = results[0]?.message_id?.toString();
+ 
+             return {
+                 success,
+                 messageId,
+                 error: success ? undefined : "Failed to send to any chat"
+             };
+         } catch (error) {
+             return {
+                 success: false,
+                 error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)
+             };
+         }
+     }
+ }
```

```diff
- 
+ import { TwitterApi } from "twitter-api-v2";
+ import { BroadcastResult } from "../types";
+ 
+ export class TwitterBroadcastClient {
+     private client: TwitterApi;
+ 
+     constructor(bearerToken: string) {
+         this.client = new TwitterApi(bearerToken);
+     }
+ 
+     async broadcast(message: string): Promise<BroadcastResult> {
+         try {
+             const cleanMessage = message.replace(/\[BROADCAST:[^\]]+\]\s*/, '');
+ 
+             const tweet = await this.client.v2.tweet({
+                 text: cleanMessage
+             });
+ 
+             return {
+                 success: true,
+                 messageId: tweet.data.id,
+             };
+         } catch (error) {
+             return {
+                 success: false,
+                 error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)
+             };
+         }
+     }
+ }
```

_****_

Now let's create the createMessage action:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ import { BroadcastClient } from "../../types";
+ 
+ export interface CreateMessageParams {
+     documentId: string;
+     client?: BroadcastClient;
+     maxLength?: number;
+     prompt?: string;
+ }
+ 
+ export interface CreateMessageResult {
+     success: boolean;
+     broadcastId?: string;
+     error?: string;
+ }
```

---

_****_

Let's create the service implementation:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ import { IAgentRuntime, Memory, ModelClass, generateText } from "@elizaos/core";
+ import { BroadcastDB } from "../../db/operations";
+ import { CreateMessageParams, CreateMessageResult } from "./types";
+ import { randomUUID } from "node:crypto";
+ 
+ export async function createBroadcastMessage(
+     runtime: IAgentRuntime,
+     params: CreateMessageParams,
+     db: BroadcastDB
+ ): Promise<CreateMessageResult> {
+     try {
+         const client = params.client || runtime.character.settings?.defaultClient || "telegram";
+         const maxLength = params.maxLength || (client === "telegram" ? 1000 : 280);
+         const broadcastId = randomUUID();
+ 
+         // Get document content
+         const document = await runtime.memory.get(params.documentId);
+         if (!document) {
+             return {
+                 success: false,
+                 error: `Document not found: ${params.documentId}`
+             };
+         }
+ 
+         // Use character's broadcast prompt if available
+         const basePrompt = params.prompt ||
+             runtime.character.settings?.broadcastPrompt ||
+             "Create a single focused message about what you learned from this content. Be specific about the insight, why it matters, and what it suggests.";
+ 
+         const prompt = `${basePrompt}
+ 
+ Content to analyze:
+ ${document.content.text}
+ 
+ Additional requirements:
+ - Message must be exactly ${maxLength} characters
+ ${client === "telegram" ? "- You may include more detail and context" : ""}
+ 
+ [BROADCAST_REQUEST:${broadcastId}]`;
+ 
+         const broadcastText = await generateText({
+             runtime,
+             context: prompt,
+             modelClass: ModelClass.SMALL,
+             maxSteps: 1
+         });
+ 
+         // Extract the actual broadcast message from between the tags if present
+         const messageMatch = broadcastText.match(/\[BROADCAST:.*?\](.*?)(?=\[|$)/s);
+         const finalText = messageMatch ? messageMatch[1].trim() : broadcastText.trim();
+ 
+         // Store in database
+         const id = db.createBroadcast(params.documentId, client, finalText);
+ 
+         return {
+             success: true,
+             broadcastId: id
+         };
+     } catch (error) {
+         return {
+             success: false,
+             error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)
+         };
+     }
+ }
```

---

_****_

Let's create the action entry point:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ import { Action, IAgentRuntime, Memory } from "@elizaos/core";
+ import { BroadcastDB } from "../../db/operations";
+ import { createBroadcastMessage } from "./service";
+ import { CreateMessageParams } from "./types";
+ 
+ export const createMessageAction: Action = {
+     name: "CREATE_BROADCAST",
+     description: "Creates a new broadcast message from a document",
+     parameters: {
+         documentId: {
+             type: "string",
+             description: "ID of the document to create broadcast from"
+         },
+         client: {
+             type: "string",
+             description: "Client to create broadcast for (telegram or twitter)",
+             optional: true
+         },
+         maxLength: {
+             type: "number",
+             description: "Maximum length of the broadcast message",
+             optional: true
+         },
+         prompt: {
+             type: "string",
+             description: "Custom prompt for generating the broadcast message",
+             optional: true
+         }
+     },
+     handler: async (
+         runtime: IAgentRuntime,
+         message: Memory,
+         state: unknown,
+         options: { [key: string]: unknown } = {}
+     ): Promise<boolean> => {
+         const db = new BroadcastDB(runtime.db);
+         const params = message.content as CreateMessageParams;
+ 
+         const result = await createBroadcastMessage(runtime, params, db);
+ 
+         if (!result.success) {
+             runtime.logger.error("Failed to create broadcast message", {
+                 error: result.error,
+                 documentId: params.documentId
+             });
+             return false;
+         }
+ 
+         runtime.logger.info("Created broadcast message", {
+             broadcastId: result.broadcastId,
+             documentId: params.documentId,
+             client: params.client
+         });
+ 
+         return true;
+     }
+ };
```

_****_

Let's create the processQueue action types:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ import { BroadcastClient } from "../../types";
+ 
+ export interface ProcessQueueParams {
+     client?: BroadcastClient;
+     maxRetries?: number;
+     retryDelay?: number;
+ }
+ 
+ export interface ProcessQueueResult {
+     success: boolean;
+     processedCount: number;
+     failedCount: number;
+     error?: string;
+ }
```

---

_****_

Let's create the processQueue service:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ import { IAgentRuntime } from "@elizaos/core";
+ import { BroadcastDB } from "../../db/operations";
+ import { ProcessQueueParams, ProcessQueueResult } from "./types";
+ import { TelegramBroadcastClient } from "../../clients/telegram";
+ import { TwitterBroadcastClient } from "../../clients/twitter";
+ import { BroadcastClient } from "../../types";
+ 
+ const DEFAULT_MAX_RETRIES = 3;
+ const DEFAULT_RETRY_DELAY = 1000;
+ 
+ async function sleep(ms: number): Promise<void> {
+     return new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(resolve, ms));
+ }
+ 
+ export async function processBroadcastQueue(
+     runtime: IAgentRuntime,
+     params: ProcessQueueParams,
+     db: BroadcastDB
+ ): Promise<ProcessQueueResult> {
+     try {
+         const maxRetries = params.maxRetries || DEFAULT_MAX_RETRIES;
+         const retryDelay = params.retryDelay || DEFAULT_RETRY_DELAY;
+         let processedCount = 0;
+         let failedCount = 0;
+ 
+         // Initialize clients
+         const clients: Partial<Record<BroadcastClient, TelegramBroadcastClient | TwitterBroadcastClient>> = {};
+ 
+         if (!params.client || params.client === "telegram") {
+             const botToken = runtime.character.settings?.secrets?.TELEGRAM_BOT_TOKEN;
+             const chatIds = runtime.character.settings?.secrets?.TELEGRAM_CHAT_ID?.split(",").map(id => id.trim()) || [];
+ 
+             if (botToken && chatIds.length > 0) {
+                 clients.telegram = new TelegramBroadcastClient(botToken, chatIds);
+             }
+         }
+ 
+         if (!params.client || params.client === "twitter") {
+             const bearerToken = runtime.character.settings?.secrets?.TWITTER_BEARER_TOKEN;
+ 
+             if (bearerToken) {
+                 clients.twitter = new TwitterBroadcastClient(bearerToken);
+             }
+         }
+ 
+         // Process each client's queue
+         for (const [clientName, client] of Object.entries(clients)) {
+             let retryCount = 0;
+ 
+             while (retryCount < maxRetries) {
+                 const broadcast = db.getNextPendingBroadcast(clientName as BroadcastClient);
+                 if (!broadcast) break;
+ 
+                 try {
+                     const result = await client.broadcast(broadcast.content);
+ 
+                     if (result.success) {
+                         db.updateBroadcastStatus(broadcast.id, "sent", Date.now());
+                         processedCount++;
+                         retryCount = 0; // Reset retry count on success
+                     } else {
+                         db.updateBroadcastStatus(broadcast.id, "failed");
+                         failedCount++;
+                         retryCount++;
+ 
+                         runtime.logger.error(`Failed to send broadcast: ${result.error}`, {
+                             broadcastId: broadcast.id,
+                             client: clientName,
+                             attempt: retryCount
+                         });
+ 
+                         await sleep(retryDelay);
+                     }
+                 } catch (error) {
+                     db.updateBroadcastStatus(broadcast.id, "failed");
+                     failedCount++;
+                     retryCount++;
+ 
+                     runtime.logger.error("Error processing broadcast", {
+                         error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error),
+                         broadcastId: broadcast.id,
+                         client: clientName,
+                         attempt: retryCount
+                     });
+ 
+                     await sleep(retryDelay);
+                 }
+             }
+         }
+ 
+         return {
+             success: failedCount === 0,
+             processedCount,
+             failedCount
+         };
+     } catch (error) {
+         return {
+             success: false,
+             processedCount: 0,
+             failedCount: 0,
+             error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)
+         };
+     }
+ }
```

---

_****_

Let's create the processQueue action entry point:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ import { Action, IAgentRuntime, Memory } from "@elizaos/core";
+ import { BroadcastDB } from "../../db/operations";
+ import { processBroadcastQueue } from "./service";
+ import { ProcessQueueParams } from "./types";
+ 
+ export const processQueueAction: Action = {
+     name: "PROCESS_BROADCAST_QUEUE",
+     description: "Process pending broadcast messages in the queue",
+     parameters: {
+         client: {
+             type: "string",
+             description: "Client to process broadcasts for (telegram or twitter)",
+             optional: true
+         },
+         maxRetries: {
+             type: "number",
+             description: "Maximum number of retries for failed broadcasts",
+             optional: true
+         },
+         retryDelay: {
+             type: "number",
+             description: "Delay in milliseconds between retries",
+             optional: true
+         }
+     },
+     handler: async (
+         runtime: IAgentRuntime,
+         message: Memory,
+         state: unknown,
+         options: { [key: string]: unknown } = {}
+     ): Promise<boolean> => {
+         const db = new BroadcastDB(runtime.db);
+         const params = message.content as ProcessQueueParams;
+ 
+         const result = await processBroadcastQueue(runtime, params, db);
+ 
+         if (!result.success) {
+             runtime.logger.error("Failed to process broadcast queue", {
+                 error: result.error,
+                 processedCount: result.processedCount,
+                 failedCount: result.failedCount
+             });
+             return false;
+         }
+ 
+         runtime.logger.info("Processed broadcast queue", {
+             processedCount: result.processedCount,
+             failedCount: result.failedCount,
+             client: params.client
+         });
+ 
+         return true;
+     }
+ };
```

---

_****_

Finally, let's create the plugin entry point:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ import { Plugin } from "@elizaos/core";
+ import { createMessageAction } from "./actions/createMessage";
+ import { processQueueAction } from "./actions/processQueue";
+ import { initializeBroadcastSchema } from "./db/schema";
+ 
+ const plugin: Plugin = {
+     name: "broadcast",
+     version: "0.1.0",
+     actions: [
+         createMessageAction,
+         processQueueAction
+     ],
+     initialize: async (runtime) => {
+         // Initialize database schema
+         initializeBroadcastSchema(runtime.db);
+ 
+         runtime.logger.info("Broadcast plugin initialized");
+         return true;
+     }
+ };
+ 
+ export default plugin;
```

---

---

_****_

I've created the broadcast plugin with the following structure and features:

1. Core Components:
   - Database schema and operations for managing broadcasts
   - Support for multiple clients (Telegram and Twitter)
   - Character-specific broadcast settings
   - Message length customization per platform

2. Actions:
   - `CREATE_BROADCAST`: Creates a new broadcast message from a document
   - `PROCESS_BROADCAST_QUEUE`: Processes pending broadcasts for specified clients

3. Client Implementations:
   - Telegram client using the Telegraf library
   - Twitter client using the twitter-api-v2 library

4. Configuration:
   - Client-specific settings (max length, formatting)
   - Retry mechanisms for failed broadcasts
   - Custom broadcast prompts per character

The plugin is now ready for testing. Would you like me to help you:
1. Install the dependencies
2. Add the plugin to your character configuration
3. Test the broadcast functionality

Or is there something specific you'd like to focus on first?

_**User**_

does the new plugin need registering with the workspace?

---

_**Assistant**_

Yes, since we're using a workspace-based setup (as indicated by the `"workspace:*"` references in package.json), we need to install dependencies and rebuild the workspace. According to the core project rules provided:

1. First install dependencies:
```bash
pnpm install --no-frozen-lockfile
```

2. Then build the workspace:
```bash
pnpm build
```

Let me help you run these commands:

---

_****_

